 P. 130. L. 20.—**वरदः** is part of the predicate of the sentence. Compare the construction of 77 **तपःफ़लचिकीर्षतः** P. 145. L. 7.

 P. 130. L. 26.**—साङ्गोपाङ्गोपनिषदः**. There is a play here upon the words Veda and Dhanurveda as if the latter, the science of using the bow, consisted of the same parts and required the same helps as the Veda itself,' Schlegel.

 P. 131. L. 6. **–हतमेव सदा मेने.** Compare **हतौतौविद्धि राक्षसौ** P. 59. L. 22.

 P. 131, L. 15.—**भैः.** The classical form is **भैषीः,**which occur in P. 137. L. 9.

 P. 131. L. 20. —**न भविष्यसि.** 'Shalt live on longer.' So Virgil says Troja fuit-Troy was' in the sense of Troy has been destroyed.'

 P. 132. L. 3.**—क्व च ते क्षत्रियचल क्वच ब्रह्मबलं महत्.** 'What is the might of the warrior in which you trust to the great power of the Brah- mana.'

 P. 132. L. 4.— The names of many of these weapons, which are my- thical and partly allegorical, have accurred in Canto XXIX. The general signification of the story is clear enough. It is a contest for a supremacy between the regal or military order and Brahminical or priestly authority, like one of those struggles which our own Europe saw in the middle ages when without employing warlike weapons the priesthood frequently gained the victory.' Schlegel quoted by Griffith,

 P. 132. LL. 21-26 are printed by Schlegel as three verses of two lines each. Taking them so he makes one sentence end with **तदद्भुतमिवाभवत्**

which words he refers to the preceding clause. But the 'miracle' is the way in which the darts were swallowed up. Translato: 'Then by (lit: in) Vasishtha was exhibited a wonder: all these weapons did the son of Brahma swallow up with his simple staff. It is possiblo however that **वसिष्ठे जपतां वरे**is to be construed with **चिक्षेप.**—There is a curious parallel to **दण्डेन ग्रसते**in the story of the Exodus from Egypt. 'And Moses and Aaron went in unto Pharoah, and they did so as the Lord had commanded; and Aaron cast down his rod before Pharoah, and before his servants, and it became a serpent. Then Pharoah also called the wise men and the sorcerers; now the magicians of Egypt they did in like manner with their enchantments. For they cast down every man his rod, and they became serpents; but Aaron's rod swallowed up their rods.' Exodus VII. 10-12.

 P. 133. L. 8. — **तेजो धारय तेजसा.** Compare **धारयिष्याम्यहं तेजस्ते-जसि** (Bomb. Ed.**तेजसा**) P. 91. L. 5.

 P. 131, LL. 7-8.—Now that I have undergone so great a penance they recognise me as a Râjarshi, the gods and rishis; not yet, I ween, has my penance obtaind its fruit.

 P. 134, L. 12.—'Tris'anku was the seventh king of Ayodhya from Ikshváku, Das'aratha being the thirty-fourth. There is nothing surprising in Vasishṭha and Vis'vâmitra being put as far back as Tris'anku, as we know that certain hymns of the Veda are ascribed to them. But it is surprising to find them both represented as still living in Râma's time.' Schelgel.

 P. 134. L. 14.—**परां गतिम् स्वर्गम्.** Compare P. 1. L. 4.

 P. 134. L. 19.— **शतं परमभास्वरम्** is in apposition to **वसिष्टपुत्रान्** ' He saw Vasishtha's sons—a glorious century.'

 P. 134. L. 21.—**महात्मानः**. So also the Bomb. Ed. The vowel is lengthened to suit the verse, Compare अनृदकेP. 58. L. 1.

 P. 135. L. 13.—**शाखान्तरम्.** ‘Another School.**' याजनादिना रक्षान्तरम्.** The expression must not be taken strictly, as Vasislitha's sons would naturally, as Muir observes (Skt. Txts. Vol. I. P. 401.), belong to the same 'school' as himself. But Tris'anku is blamed in general terms for the hope betrayed by his application to them, of getting elsewhere the assistance denied to him by Vasishtha.

 P. 135. L. 16.**—चोवाच** is perhaps a correction for the reading of the Bomb. Ed**.सोवाच,**an irregular sandhi, which is however found elsewhere.

 P. 136. L. 19. —Take**त्रैलोक्यस्यापि** with **याजने. त्रैलोक्यस्यापि सिद्धार्थमिय्यर्थः** 'He can perform even that great sacrifice.' That is, if he says the sacrifice yon . desire is impossible, it must be impossible.

 P. 136. L. 24. — **घोराभिसंहितम् घोराभिप्रायसंयुक्तम्.**

 P. 135. L. 26. — **स्वं स्वम्.** Translate; 'Each his own.'

 P. 136. L. 2. – **चित्यमाल्याङ्गरागश्च चिता (चित्य** in text ) **इमशानं वन भवं पुष्पभस्मादि माल्याङ्गरागो यस्य.**

 P. 136. L. 3. – **स्यज्य.** Against the common rule.

 P. 136. L. 7. – **विफलीकृतम्.** Not in the sense in which it is used in P. 118. L. b, but ‘baffled, foiled.' **विफलीकृतं वसिष्ठपुत्रेर्विनाशितैहिकामुष्मि कार्यम्.** Cf. below **तच्च नावाप्यते फलम्.** L. 18.

 P. 136. L. 17. — **दर्शनम्.** 'purpose.' Comparo the corresponding use of our word view.

 P. 136. I. 19. — **अनृतं नोक्तपूर्वंमे ऋतुशतं न कृतं प्वयेति चेत्तत्राह अनृतमिति.** It is more natural to suppose that the reforence is to his general truthfulness.

 P. 136. L. 23. — **प्रयत मानस्य** i.e. **मम.**

 P. 137. L. 8.—**इक्ष्वाको** Ikshvaku being used as a family name as well as the proper name of the head of the race. Compare P. 141. L 28; and see P. 154 L 7 for a similar use of **जनक.**

 P. 137. L. 11. —**यज्ञसाह्यम् यज्ञसाहाय्यम्.**

 P. 137. L. 14. — Compare P. 131. L. 6.

 P. 137. L. 21.– **अनादृतम्** is to be taken with **आख्येयम्** in the sense of 'without regard i.c, to any such considerations as that of offending and the like. The Bomb. Ed. Com. explains it differently. **अनादृतम् उपेक्षारूपं चण्डालयाजनरूपं निन्दात्मकं वा यद्वाक्यम्.**

 P. 137. I. 27. — **महोदयम् तन्नामानमृषिम्.** Compare **वासिष्ठाः सर्वे समहोदयाः** P. 138. L. 8 and L. 26. Schlegel takes it as a name of Vasishtha, which does not seem right, as Vasishtha does not seem to be involved in the destruction of his hundered sons and Mahodaya. It may be, as Böthlingk and Roth suggest, the name of one of the sous.

 P. 138. L. 14. – **मृतपाः शववस्त्रादिहारिणः**

 P. 138. LL. 14-15. — Compare P. 144. L. 6.

 P. 139. L. 18. — **चकारावाहनम्** — 'gummoned' — takes an accusative **सर्वाः देवताः** like the simple verb.

 P. 140. L. 3.**—भूयः.** 'Back.' Compare a similar use of **पुनर्.** L. 5. below.

 P. 140. L. 6.—**त्राहि**. See note on P. 110. L. 20.

 P. 140. L. 9**—योगात्**. See note on P. 129. L. 23.

 P. 140. L. 13.**—लोका वा स्यादनिन्दकः.** Or there shall be a world without an Indra.' He does not threaten to dethrone the Indra of the existing world as Schlegel and Griffith translate. Compare **अनिन्द्रं लोकमिच्छान्ती.** P. 70. L. 16. and note there.

 P. 140. L. 24.—It seeins natural to recogniso with Schlegel in this legend the result of the surprise with which the Aryans, as they spread southward, saw strange stars rising above the horizon.

 P. 141. L. 14.—This is a great hindrance to our penance which has overspread the southern quarter.' **अयम्**is attracted into the same gender as the word to which it refers. This cannot refer to the events just related; for, Vis'vâmitra was successful in the sacrifice perforined for Trisanku,' Schlegel. But Vis'vâmitra had been in the course or the events betrayed into anger to the interruption of his tapus.

 P. 141. L. 16.— **पश्चिमस्याम्.** Sc. **दिशि.** The other form **पश्चिमायाम्**P. 99. L. 21.—**विशालायाम्.** Vis'ala is here the name of a river, and must be distinguished from the विशाला पुरीP. 109. L. 22.

 P. 141, L. 21.—**अम्वरीषः.** 'Ambarisha is the twenty-ninth from Ikshvâku (canto LXX. 40.) IIis reign is therefore separated by an immense interval of time from the things that befell Trisanku Richika too, who is represented in this canto (v. 11, and following) as having grown up sons while Ambarisha was still reigning, and who was himself a son of Bhrigu and one of the oldest of the Rishis, as having married the eldest sister of Visvâmitra. All this is sufficient to show that Indian mythology is one perpetual anachronism, everything moving in a circle' Schlegel.

 P. 141, L. 22.—**पशुमिन्द्रो जहार ह .** Compare the legend of Sagara's sacrifice. P. 96. L. 25,

 P. 141. L. 26. – **प्रायश्चित्तम् प्रायश्चित्तस्य कारणम्. — नरं वा** with **पशुम्.** 'A fit victim even though it be a man.'

 P. 141, L. 28.—**इक्ष्वाकुः.** See note on P. 37. L. S.

 P. 142. L. 8.—**पशोरर्थे**. ‘For a victim.

 P. 142. L. 10.—**इतः.** 'Of these.'

 P. 142. L. 18.**—रक्षे. रक्ष्**is generally conjugated in the Parasmaipada,

 P. 142. L. 20.—**शुनःशुपः.** From the Bomb. Ed.—Schlegel **शुनह्शोफ़ः.**

 P. 142. L. 22.—**विक्रीतं मध्यमं मन्ये.** T'he middle one is already sold I think.' Cf. **हतौ तौ विद्धि राक्षसौ**P. 50. L. 22.—'In the mythical story related in this and the following canto we may discover, I think, some indication of the epoch at which the immolation of lower animals was substituted for human sacrifice...So when Iphigeneia was about to be sacrificed at Aulis, one legend tells us that a hind was substituted for the virgin.' Gorresio, quoted by Griffith. The words नरं वाP. 141. L. 26. perhaps point to the fact that the animal was to take the place of a hu- man offering. Griffith aptly cites also the story of the sacrifice of Isaac.

 P. 143. L. 5**.—मातुलम्**. Sec P. 87. L. 10 and compare note on P. 141. L. 21.

 P. 143, L. 13.— **सः.** Sec note on P. 32. L. 3. **त्वम्**is understood here; or rather perhaps the origina signification of the verbal termination is still so far felt that it is possibe to join with it the demonstrative pronoun. Muir (Skt Txts V. 406) has a reading for: which I do not find elsewhere. Gorresio has **नाथो मे स्वमनाथस्य.**

 P. 143. L. 18.—**परलोकहितार्थाय**is inserted parenthetically botween the **यस्कृते**and the **तस्य**it explains. That for which-advantage in the other world-parents beget children.'

 P. 143. L. 20.—**गीवितमात्रेण.** 'Iis life alone i. e. seek not to please me or obtain merit for me in any other way.

 P. 143. L. 28.**—स्वमांसमिव भोजने.** 'As if a man were to eat his own flesh.' The reading of the Bomb. Ed. **स्वमांसम्**is not so good. It is taken from L. 5, on the next page (where also however Gorresio reads **स्वमांसम्**) but there seems to be an intentional play upon the two words. For the accusative after **भोजने**compare the note on P. 15. L. 11.

 P. 144, L. 4.**—रोमहर्षेण्म्.** It seems probable that the physical mean- ing of the root **हम्**is the original one, as it is not easy to see how its use in a connection like the present could be got if the word originally meant joy. Compare **हृष्टरोमा** P'. 122. L. 10.

 P. 144. L. 15.—**गच्छामहै.** The plural where we might have looked for the dual. Cf, note on P. 70. L. 17. Bomb. has **गच्छावहे** (cf. **गच्छामहे** P. 156. L. 24.) —**गम्**is generally conjugated in the Parasmaipada.

 P. 144. L. 21.—**अग्न्याभि**: Form the Bomb. Ed.-Schlegel **अग्न्याभिः.**

 P. 146. L. 4.—**वेपन्तीम्.** This root is generally conjugated in the Atmancpada in classical Sanskrit.

 P. 146. L. 12.—**लभतां साधु.** 'Come, let him have.' A common use of **साधु.** Cf. **तथा साधु विधीयताम्** P. 10. L. 23.

 P. 146. L. 16.—**महत्त्यमृषिमुख्यस्वं ददामि.** That is he confers on him the title of Maharshi.

 P. 146. L. 20.—Bomb. Ed. reads **नाह**for **आह**. The **ततोहं विजितेन्द्रियः** would then be ironical.

 P. 147. LL. 14-21 are arranged by Schlegel as four verses of two lines each.

 P. 147. L. 15.—**उत्सृजते.** Bomb. Ed. **उत्स्रक्ष्यते.** The present is naturally used for a future whose certainty it is desirable to emphasize. Cf. **विनाशयति त्रैलोवयम्** P. 149. L. 18. — **सृज**is generally construed in the Pa rasmaipada in classical Sanskrit.

 P. 147. L. 20.—**कोकिलः….अहम्.** 'I in the form of the cuckoo that takes the ravished heart in spring when the trees are green' (i. e. at this time.) It seems better to take **माधवे रुचिरे** more closely with **हृदयग्राही**than with **स्थास्यानि**. Rainbhâ is assured that she will have three potent allies:— the notes of the cuckoo, the charms of spring, and the presence of the god of love. Compare:-

'Your tongue's sweet air

More tuneable than lark to shepherd's ear,

When wheat is green, when hawthorn buds appear.'

Midsummer Night's Dream. Act I, Scene I.

 P. 147. L. 22.**—वहुगुणम् हावभावादिगुणोपेतम्**. Cf. L. 24.

 P. 147. L. 23**.—भेदयस्व नपस्विनम्.** 'Separate the ascetic,' i. e. from his asceticism. So 'seduce him,' by which we may translate it means literally 'lead him away.' Bomb. Ed. Com. **कामोत्पादनेन तपसश्चालय.**

 P. 148. L. 11.— **रम्भा शैली तदाभवत्.** Compare the story of Lot's wife, who was punished by being transformed into a pillar of salt. Genesis XIX. V. 26.

 P. 148, L. 15.—Schlegel marks the omission of a line and a half after **वभूवास्य पुनश्चिन्ता.** I have supplied **तपोपहरणे कृते**from Carey and M. and the Bomb. Ed. and printed the three lines as one verse.

 P. 148. L. 18.—**आत्मानम्.** ‘Myself' i. e. 'my body'. Comparo noto on P. 108. L. 13.

 P. 149. L. 3.—**आनिष्ठत.** Translate: Was still performing.'

 P. 149. L. 8.—**निःशेषिते.निरवशेषतो दत्ते.** Rather, 'All eaten.'

 P. 149. L. 22.—**न प्रतिजानीमः.** Böhtlingk and R. seem to be right in translating 'If we do not consent'. Bomb. Ed. snys of: is equal to **प्रतिक्रियां न जानीमः.** Carey and Marshman, translate 'We cannot vouch that mankind will not become atheists.'

 P. 149. L. 28.— Schlegel translates **यथा दह्यते देवराज्यं चिकीर्षेत**As of yore the world was burned so (i. e. with similar destructive conse- quences he may &c.)' But this does not seem right. The first clause is complete in itself. The three worlds are burning as of old they burned &c.**'—देवराज्यं चिकीर्षेत.** 'He may even aim at lordship over the gods. Bomb. Ed. Com. **यद्यसौ देवराज्यमपि चिकीर्षेंत तदा तदप्यस्य दीयतामित्यर्थ इति केचित्। यद्यस्याभीष्टं न दीयते तदासौ देवराज्यं चिकीर्षतातोस्य यन्मनस्तस्स्थंब्रह्मर्षित्वं तद्दीयतामित्यर्थ इत्यन्ये।** The second of these interpretations seems preferable, as the sea can hardly refer to anything but Visvamitra's desire to bo a Brahmarshi.

 P. 150. L. 3.—**स्म.** An epic form for **स्मः.**

 P. 150. L. 6.—**स्वस्ति.** As an accusative.

 P. 150. L. 10. — **ओमिति ब्रह्मज्ञानसाधनं वषडिति यज्ञसाधनं वेदाश्चतदपेक्षिसाङ्गोपाङ्गादिप्रतिपादका**

 P. 150. L. 12.—**एवं वदनु**. So Vasishṭha says in L. 14. below **एवमस्तु.**

 P. 150. L. 15.—**ब्रह्मर्षित्वम्.** Another reading is **ब्रह्मर्षिस्स्वम्.**

 P. 151. L. 7.**—तृप्तिः…कथानां नास्ति.** Compare **वुभुक्षितानां दीनानां नाहमिरुपलभ्यते**P. 39. L. 2.

 P. 152. L. 2—**त्वयि.**'With you,' 'apud te.' Compare **इह**1. 6. and **पूर्वके**L. 18. below.

 P. 152. L. 3.—**कृतकामौ** is used proleptically, that is to say, it refers to a time which is not the time of the sentence in which it stands, but in advance of that. Translate ' show them this bow, I entreat thee, and (0) give them their wish.' Or the ccnstruction may be imitated in the translation 'show the gratified princes the bow.'

 P. 152. L. 6.**—श्रुयतामस्य धनुषः.** For the construction compare **दुहितुः... वक्तुमर्हसि.** P. 90. L. 10.

 P. 152. L. 7.—**देवरात इति ख्यातः......तस्य.** It is not necessary to supply in this and similar passages’there was’. The first line, though standing in grammatical independence, is in sense subordinate to the second, so that—the idiom not being an English one — **देवरात…तस्य**must be translated as if it were **देवरातस्य.** The idiom is a common onein Marathi. Compare also note on P. 59. L. 8.

 P. 152. L. 9.— **दक्षयज्ञवधे.** 'Daksha was one of the ancient Progenitors or Prajapatis created by Brahma, The sacrifice which is here spoken of, and in which S'iva smote the gods because he had not been invited to share the sacred oblations with them, seems to refer to the origin of the worship of S'iva, to its increase, and to the struggle, it maintained with other older forms of worship.' Griffith from Gorresio.

 P. 132. I. 20. —**शोधयता** i. o. **मया.**

 P. 153. L. 7.—**आत्मानम्. स्वं स्वमात्मानम्.**—Bom. Ed. has **मै**for **तै**in this line.

 P. 153. L. 8.—**पीडयन्.** The augment omitted. So also three lines below **प्रसादयम.**

 P. 153. L. 14.— **वीर्यसंदिग्धाः. संदिग्धवीर्याः.आहिताग्न्यादित्वान्निष्ठायाः परनिपातः.**The compound **कौशल्यासुप्रजः** P. 65. L. 11. If the reading there is right might be compared with this. But it is better to take **वीर्यसंदिग्धाः** as a tatpurusha compound, with **संदिग्धाः** in the sense of 'doubting.'

 P. 153. L. 18.— So in the story of the Odyssey Penelope promises to marry the man who can string the bow of Ulysses.

 P. 153. L. 25.— **प्राविशन्पुरीम्** and **निर्जग्मुः.** The palace is outside the city.

 P. 154. L. 7.— **जनकैः.** 'Janaka' used as a family name. Compare the similar use of Ikshvâku P. 137. L. 8.

 P. 154, L. 8.—**पुरितम्.** The fuller phrase **पुरयस्व शरेण**P. 169. L. 26.

 P. 154. L. 9.—**नैतस्सुरगणाः सर्वे** as if **शक्ताः** had stood in the preceding line.

 P. 154. L. 25.— To lift the bow (**ग्रहणम्**) is a great achievement, to hold it (**तोलनम्**) is still more difficult, to string it (**आरोपणम्**) still

more so, and hardest of all is the task of fitting it with an arrow (**पूरंणम्**) Rama docs all four, and moreever breaks the bow.

 P. 155. L. 10.**—सीता प्राणैर्चदुमता प्राणैः** is not for **प्राणेभ्यः** as the Bomb. Ed. Com. says. The expression means literally 'Sita whom I think highly of even when she is put alongside of (for comparison) life'; i. e. dear as life itself to me.' Compare note on P. 56, L. 20.

 P. 155. L. 13.— **प्रश्रितेः.** Schlegel :. So also below L. 26.

 P. 156. L. 6.— **पुत्रकैः.** Plural where the dual would be put in classical Sanskrit. So **आत्मजैः सह आनयस्व**P. 159. L. 8. See the note on P. 70. L. 17. The Bomb. Ed. explains it as the plural of respect, referring only to Rama. But compare **पुत्रयोरुभयोरेव**L. 14. below.

 P. 156. L. 24.— **गच्छामहे.** In the Atmanepada. See note on P. 144. L. 15. For the use of the present tense compare note on P. 147. L. 15.

 P. 157. L. 18.— **आप्स्यसे. आप्.** is not conjugated in the Atmauepada in classical Sanskrit. Bomb. Ed. has **लप्स्यसे.** Compare **उपलप्स्यसे**P. 156. L. 14.

 P. 157. L. 27.— **प्रतिग्रहो दातृवशः.** 'The receiver (i. e. of a bride, compare **सुराप्रतिग्रहात्**P. 111. L. 23. ) is at the giver's disposal' Cf. P. 111. L. 20. 'The Bomb. Ed. Com. **प्रतिग्रहः कन्यागवादीनां दातृवशः यदि दाता ददाति तदा प्रतिग्राह्यं प्रतिग्रहीचेति स्थितः.**

 P. 158. L. 18. — **वार्याफलकपर्यन्ताम्. वार्यामलकपर्यन्तामिति पाढे वार्या मलका भामलकविशेषाः पर्यन्तेषु यस्या इत्यर्थः**

 P. 159. L. 7.— **इक्ष्वाकुम्**. See note on P. 137. L. 8.

 P. 159. L. 8— **आत्मजैः. सह**See note on P. 156. L. 6.

 P. 159. L. 17.—**विदितं ते. ...वक्ता वसिष्ठः. '**You know that Vasistha is our spokesman.

 P. 159, L. 23.—Vasishṭha begins by an account of the genealogy of those on behalf of whom he seeks the daughter of Janaka. Compare P. 161. L. 23.

 P. 160. L. 12.— **प्रतिराजानः शत्रुभुता राजानः— प्रतिराजानः** would be **प्रतिराजाः** in classical Sanskrit.

 P. 160. L. 13.— **शशिविन्दवः.** Bomb. Ed. **शशविन्दवः.**

 P. 160. L. 14.— **सः** i. e. **असितः.**

 P. 160. L. 19.— **अतिरतः.** Bomb. Ed. **अभिरतः.**

 P. 160. L. 23. — **अभ्युपागम्या शरणं गत्वा.** In the next line **पुत्रजन्मनि** goes with **अभ्यवदत्.** 'Concerning the birth of a son'

 P. 161. I. 1. — **गरः... दत्तः... सह तेन.** Conpare for the construction P. 152. L. 7. and the note there.

 P. 161. I. 18.— **सदृशाभ्यां... सदृशे**. 'Lilke to lilke.' Compare P. 163. L. 19.

 P. 161. L. 28. — **प्रथमो जनकः** 'The first Janaka' See note on P. 154. I.7.

 P. 162. L. 25. — **प्रेषयामास.** 'Sent to say’.

 P. 162. L. 27. — **तस्य** Bomb Ed. Com. **उक्तवस्तुद्वयस्य.** Better with **युद्धमासीन्मया सह.**

 P. 162. L. 28.— **अभिमुखः.** Bomb Ed. **विमुखः**explained as meaning **युद्धविमुखः.**

 P. 163. L. 12. — **उत्तरे.** Supply **दिवसे.** Compare next page L. 11. The marriage is to take place on the third day from that day (Cf P. 164. L. 28. and P. 165. L. 21.), which will be the further or second ( **उत्तरे** ) of the two days when the moon is in Phalgunî. With the construction **फाल्गुन्यामुत्तरे** may be compared the expression **फल्गुनीपूर्वसमये** which Böhtlingk and R. quote from Mahâbh. 13. 3264. The Bomb, Ed. has the same reading as that in the text except that it has तृतीय दिवसे and फल्गुन्वाम्. Gorresio reads, with Carey and M.

वर्तन्तेद्य यथा राजन् दिवसे तुत्तरे पुनः।  
फाल्गुण्यः प्रतिपत्स्यन्ते विवाहस्तत्र नोस्त्वय॥

This reading evidently contemplates the day immediately following maghd as the day for the wedding, and accordingly find that Gorresio's text has **पुत्राणां प्रियपुत्रः सः** for our **प्रभाते काल्पमुत्थाय** P. 164. L. 28, and so makes the godâna take place on the same evening, and the mar- riage on the following day. According to some later authorities Bhaga was the lord not of the Uttara, but of the Pârva Phalgunî, and the Bomb. Ed. Com. tries to reconcile that view with his text:— अ**द्य तृतीय दिवसे तय मिथिलाप्रवेशात्तृतीयदिवसे यज्ञसमाप्तेस्तृतीय दिघसे वाद्य मघानक्षत्रम्॥ फल्गुन्यां पूर्वफल्गुनी नक्षत्रे॥ उत्तरे श्रष्टे॥ अत एव भगो यत्र प्रजापतिरित्यनेन अविरोधः॥ भगो हि पुर्वफल्गुनी देवः। उत्तरफल्गुन्यास्त्वयमीत बोध्यम्॥ वैवाहिकं विवाहम्॥ विनयादित्वात् ठक्॥ मघानक्षत्रं पितरीदेवता फल्गुनीनक्षत्रमर्यमाठेवता फल्गुनीनक्षत्रं भगो देवतेति तैत्तिरीयसंहितायाम्॥ अर्यम्णः पूर्वं फल्गुनी भगस्योत्तरे इति तत्ब्राह्मणे चोक्तत्वेन यथाश्रुतमंदसम्यागति तत्वम्॥ उत्तरे इति पुंस्त्वमार्षम्॥**

 P. 163. L. 20.—'Of Sîta and Urmild with Rama and Lakshmana respectively.'

 P. 164. L. 11.— **उत्तरे दिवसे…फ़ाल्गुनीभ्याम्.** See note on P. 163. L. 12. The dual is not to be taken as referring to both nakshatras. It is used, along with the singular, (found in the previous passage), or the plural, as the name of either nakshatra. There is a special sutra for the use of the instrumental caso alongside of the locative which is used in the previous passage. Gorresio and Carey and M. have here.

उत्तरे दिवसे ब्रह्मन् फाल्गुण्यो ( ण्ये

C. and M.

) भगदेवताः।  
विवाहेषु प्रशंसन्ति नक्षत्रं वै विपश्चितः॥

 P. 164, L. 16.— **आस्येताम्**is a very irregular and suspicious form of the 2nd pers. dual of the Potential. Bomb. Ed. has **आस्यताम्**

 P. 164. L. 25.— **आपृष्ट्वा.** Against the common rule. The Bomb. Ed. has this form here, and also in the passage at P. 168. L. 2.

 P. 164. L. 28.— **काल्पम्.** From the Bomb. Edition. Schlegel has **काल्यम्.**

 P. 165. LL. 23-28. are arranged by Schlegel in three verses of two lines each, Bomb. Ed. Com. takes L. 23. with the preceding line. P. 166. L. 2.q. 'The marriage rite.'

 P. 166. I. 5. — **कः स्थितः प्रतिहारो मे. येन राजागमनं प्रतिबध्यते इति शेषः — संप्रतीक्षते.** Sc. **राजा.**

 P. 166. L. 19.—**छिद्रकुम्भैः** Pots pierced with holes from which the water was allowed to descend on the head. Compare **प्राक्षिपत्...जलम्**P. 167. L. 3. The Bomb. Ed. reads **अच्छिद्र**and has the following note— **त्रकुम्भैः नानावर्णादियुतकुम्भैः। अच्छिद्रकुम्मैरिति पाठे स्फुटनादिदोषरहितैः स्वर्णकुम्भैरित्यर्थ इति कतकः । अच्छिद्रकुम्भैः करकौरतिंतीर्थः॥**

 P. 168. L. 16.— **स्म**is an enclitic particle which is often used as here to give a past signification to the present tense. Compare what has been said of the nature of the augment on P. 49. L. 28.

 P. 169. L. 2.—**ससंज्ञा इव.** i. e. even they were not quite themselves.

 P. 169. L. 24 — **गृह्य.** Against the common rule.

 P. 169. L. 25.— **जामदग्न्यं महद्धनुः.** 'Jamadagni's great bow.' Cf. P. 171. L. 8. Notice that this more general signification of the derivative must have proceded the ordinary use as a patronymnic, which is found for example in L. 25,' below.

 P. 171. L. 12. — **उस्सादयम्.** The augment omitted.

 P. 171. L. 15.— **महन्द्रनिलयः.** Compare P. 170. L. 8. and P. 172. L. 26. Also see Raghuvans'a VI. 51.

 P. 171. L. 26.— **पितुः गौरवयन्वितकयः**. Measuring his words out of respect for his father.'

 P. 171. L. 28.— **आस्थितम्.** 'I have heard, son of Bhrigu, of the deed you did; we approve of your conduct in clearing yourself of the debt you owed to your father' Gorresio has **न भ्यसूये तस्कर्म पिनुरानुण्यकारिणः**

 P. 172. L. 5. — **सज्जम्**. Bomb El. **सज्यम्.**

 P. 172. L. 9.— **इमां त्वद्गतिम्.** SeeP. 71. L. 14.

 P. 172. L. 23.— **वसे. वस्**is generally conjugated in the Parasmaipada,

 P. 173. L. 5.—**इयम्**is of the same gender as **त्रीडा**by attraction,

 P. 173, L. 11.— **दृश्य.** Against the common rulo.

 P. 175. LL. 15-18.— 'Sitû is dear to Rama as his father's choice. Her virtues and her beauty endear her the more to him. And in her heart ever more and more her husband dwells; spite of the fleshly veil,' that separates them, their hearts speak openly one with the other.' I question if thero be anywhere in literature a finer picture of wedded love' than that contained in these closing verses.
